<div id="review_95545401" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95545401" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95545401?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95545401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9377033584271768703">Mankind finally has a way not only to defend themselves from the demons that have taken over the night, but they have the ability to combat their enemies. Arlen, aka the Warded Man, wants to distribute the combat wards he found to everyone in the world so they don't have to suffer at the hands of the demons as he did when his mother died.<br/><br/>Compare this to the Krasian method of enslaving all mankind and forcing them to fight in alagai'sharak, the Krasian's name for their nightly battle with the dem</span>
  <span id="freeText9377033584271768703" style="display:none">Mankind finally has a way not only to defend themselves from the demons that have taken over the night, but they have the ability to combat their enemies. Arlen, aka the Warded Man, wants to distribute the combat wards he found to everyone in the world so they don't have to suffer at the hands of the demons as he did when his mother died.<br><br>Compare this to the Krasian method of enslaving all mankind and forcing them to fight in alagai'sharak, the Krasian's name for their nightly battle with the demons.<br><br>In this respect, I couldn't help but compare The Desert Spear to The Matrix Reloaded. Not because there was a decrease in quality like the Matrix films, but moreso because suddenly the demons aren't as scary just like the agents lost all their spunk in the second and third films.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333350i/693289._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are so many ways and means that have been found, especially by Leesha and those of Deliverer's (formerly Cutter's) Hollow, to either combat the demons or make oneself invisible to them that it's almost like the demons aren't even there anymore. This was a little disappointing especially in a series that is all about groups of people coming together for the cause of warring with demonkind.<br><br>Luckily, there's enough going on that this isn't too big of an issue, just something that was a little disappointing.<br><br>The Desert Spear, book 2 of the Demon Cycle, begins by following Ahmann something something something Jardir, who we met in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88827544" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warded Man</a>, and exclusively deals with the events in Krasia and Jardir's history...and this lasts for about a quarter of the book.<br><br>I know many have complained about this aspect of the book, that the book takes far too long to get to Arlan, Leesha, and Rojer, but I'm a firm believer that delayed satisfaction does in fact make you appreciate your favorite parts.<br><br>But, I can't really say that I even loathed reading the first part. The more I read/listened, the more I found I was sucked into Jardir's past/present and the effort that went into creating this society.<br><br>Not only are new wards created/found, but we find out there are more demons than we have seen so far, one of them being the Mind demons, who rule all of demonkind. These guys make a couple of appearances and prove that although most demons aren't much of a threat, there are still some that could pose some difficulties, especially since they have the ability to think and reason like man.<br><br>Leesha and Rojer have become mainstays in Deliverer's Hollow where many refugees have fled to escape the flood that is the Krasians. This is where we also find out the advancements that Leesha has made on warding. Many have mentioned that Leesha is a bit of a wonder woman in this book and while that's true to an extent, I think a lot of this comes from the fact that we see Leesha through the eyes of Ahmann Jardir, who has a bit of a skewed perspective of her.<br><br>The issue of The Deliverer, or Shar'Dama Ka in Krasia, is central to The Desert Spear. While Arlan does everything he can to fight this distinction, the people of the north will believe what they want to believe, and many times to Arlen's frustration.<br><br>On the other hand, in Krasia, Ahmann Jardir not only convinces himself and Krasia that he is the Shar'Dama Ka, but takes his unified Krasian army to the north to force the people of the north to fight demonkind.<br><br><b>Audiobook Commentary</b><br><br>I realized I haven't been that good at discussing the audio portion of the book when I do an Audiobook review, so I wanted to add this section so that the review will actually be handy to those who were debating on whether to listen or read, having already made the decision to obtain this book.<br><br>Pete Bradbury does a great job in both The Desert Spear and The Warded/Painted Man audiobooks. He has a gruff voice, which works well for Arlen, Jardir, all of Krasia, Messengers, etc. But, at the same time, it doesn't even sound weird when he does the female characters' voices. The Audiobook is really well done and definitely recommended.<br><br><b>When Should You Read The Desert Spear?</b><br><br>The Desert Spear continues on the same level as The Warded Man, which I highly recommend and while the characters are great, the world that Peter V. Brett created has created a huge fan in me.<br><br>4.5 out of 5 Stars </span>
  <a data-text-id="9377033584271768703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2921122530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2921122530" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2921122530?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle">beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=brutal">brutal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2019">bb-b-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=cool-creatures">cool-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2921122530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17166211177873434673">How do I feel about The Desert Spear? <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567347005ra/28084150.gif' width='400' height='160' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In some ways I liked it more than the Warded Man. In others less.<br/><br/>It starts off really well. In the prologue we find that the Corelings seen to date are just the tip of the iceberg and there are others out there that think, plot and strategize and they’ve just taken an interest in the happening’s topside. Then we jump back in time and learn all about Jardir’s training as a boy with the Dessert tribes. We follow that tale and how he became the man that eventua</span>
  <span id="freeText17166211177873434673" style="display:none">How do I feel about The Desert Spear? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1567347005ra/28084150.gif" width="400" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In some ways I liked it more than the Warded Man. In others less.<br><br>It starts off really well. In the prologue we find that the Corelings seen to date are just the tip of the iceberg and there are others out there that think, plot and strategize and they’ve just taken an interest in the happening’s topside. Then we jump back in time and learn all about Jardir’s training as a boy with the Dessert tribes. We follow that tale and how he became the man that eventually betrays Arlen and leaves him to die.<br><br>This was an interesting side to the story. The switch up completely from the PoVs of the Warded Man was a little hard to take since I really wanted to see the old gang again. But we spend the first third of the book with the backstory of the Krasians and the rise of Jardir. It was interesting and almost felt like a different tale. Jardir’s wife who makes him the man he is today was also captivating. I wasn’t sure if she was more power hungry than him or just a believer. Either way she is a powerhouse and extremely devious. This culture too is brutal and I’m not a fan of their conquer the land rape all the breeding age women to create more sons to battle mentality. Historically accurate, probably. Fun to read, not really for me, it made me hate their culture.<br><br>I loved it when we finally got back to the trio of PoVs from the first book. But then all the drama started to happen. I’m not sure why a lot of male fantasy writers don’t do relationships in their stories well. The Desert Spear suffers from the main characters Arlen and Leesha being wanted/loved by everyone they meet and again Arlen is put in a situation where someone that was recently raped it throwing herself at him. *shakes head* no just no. It really turned a little into a sad parody of a drama. I’d rather all of the relationship stuff got left out and just focus on the main plot if you’re bad at them.<br><br>For Arlen the good things were: <br><br>The changes he is going through because of the tattoos on his skin.<br>Seeing the foster family that raised him and getting some closure there.<br>Traveling between lands to spread his wards.<br>The fight with a Coreling Prince.<br><br>The bad things were: <br><br>Every freaking relationship he has with women.<br>His refusal all the time of being the Deliverer.<br><br>For Leesha the good things were:<br><br>Her strides forward in warding and leading the village.<br>Coming to terms her mother being awful and sometimes wise, but usually in an awful way<br><br>The bad things:<br><br>Her total lack of sense when Jardir shows up<br>The drama llama that is her relationship with Jardir *ugh*<br><br>I really like the plot and fight against the corelings but the side plots of murder, rape and mayhem just wasn’t my thing and I cringed every time Leesha and Jardir talked. The sub plotting of jardir’s wife against Leesha was interesting but again I could have done without that bit of drama in the book.<br><br>Overall the world building and main plot to destroy the corelings is interesting but I think that Brett could would on interpersonal dynamics a little. Also, tone down the raping and pillaging while you are at it. Did we really need another scene with Renna and her father, like the one we got? I get it, you don’t have to rub my nose it in anymore.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17166211177873434673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98288822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98288822" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98288822?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-david-gemmell-legend">award-nominee-david-gemmell-legend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=angels-demons-heaven-hell">angels-demons-heaven-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=signed-first-or-limited-edition">signed-first-or-limited-edition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=unique-magic">unique-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98288822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10370533824514816824">4.0 to 4.5 stars. I really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3428935.The_Warded_Man__Demon_Trilogy___1_' title='The Warded Man (Demon Trilogy, #1) by Peter V. Brett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warded Man</a>, the first novel in Peter Brett's Demon Trilogy, and was really looking forward to reading this sequel. Even with high expectation, Brett does not disappoint with this second entry. Without giving away any spoilers, I will just talk about those aspects of the book that I really thought were fantastic. <br/><br/>First, one of the things I like about epic fantasy trilogies is when the plot begins fairly small and then develops into a larger and larger story </span>
  <span id="freeText10370533824514816824" style="display:none">4.0 to 4.5 stars. I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3428935.The_Warded_Man__Demon_Trilogy___1_" title="The Warded Man (Demon Trilogy, #1) by Peter V. Brett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warded Man</a>, the first novel in Peter Brett's Demon Trilogy, and was really looking forward to reading this sequel. Even with high expectation, Brett does not disappoint with this second entry. Without giving away any spoilers, I will just talk about those aspects of the book that I really thought were fantastic. <br /><br />First, one of the things I like about epic fantasy trilogies is when the plot begins fairly small and then develops into a larger and larger story as the novel unfolds. An example of this is Martin's Song of Ice and Fire which begins with a dispute among rival houses and soon escalates into a civil war and imminent invasion from without. This novel certainly has the requisite escalation of scope and tension. <br /><br />Second, I really like world-building and descriptions of other societies and customs and Brett does a superb job with his detailed narrative of the Krasians. The Krasians are brutal and many of their customs and ways are sadistic and cruel, but Brett still manages to make them three dimensional and provide an understanding (if not a justification) for their actions. Add to that the strong "hint" that the ancient past of the world was a lot more "technological" than the present and you have the makings for many more surprises to come. <br /><br />Third, I like larger-than-life characters and this book has several with the two most prominent being the Krasian leader, Jadir, and the Warded Man, Arlen. I must say that one of my favorite characters by the end of the book was Abban who begins the story as a greedy, cowardly individual and yet by the end of the story you have a tremendous amount of sympathy for him and the hint that he might have a larger role to play in the battle to come (I hope so). <br /><br />Fourth, I like intersting fantasy elements and this book has that taken care of in the form of the demon "corelings" whose number and type expand in this story. <br /><br />Overall, an excellent read and looking forward to the final book in the trilogy....so MAKE IT FAST PETER!!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10370533824514816824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1559245696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559245696" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1559245696?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2017-shelf">2017-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1559245696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5690124129624445912">For a full first third of the novel, I had to calm myself down and wonder why so much time and effort was being put into humanizing Jadir, the man who had betrayed Arlen so brutally in the first book, but I eventually got over it. The world is a big place and there have to be burly warriors to defend it. I didn't mind so much how crazily stereotypical Muslims are portrayed here because EVERYONE is heavily stereotyped in these books.<br/><br/>Hell, that's okay simply because it's a really harsh world overr</span>
  <span id="freeText5690124129624445912" style="display:none">For a full first third of the novel, I had to calm myself down and wonder why so much time and effort was being put into humanizing Jadir, the man who had betrayed Arlen so brutally in the first book, but I eventually got over it. The world is a big place and there have to be burly warriors to defend it. I didn't mind so much how crazily stereotypical Muslims are portrayed here because EVERYONE is heavily stereotyped in these books.<br /><br />Hell, that's okay simply because it's a really harsh world overrun with demons that come out every single night and people have to be hard and crazy to survive it. If that means going weird cultural directions to taking things to an extreme in order to unify or cow the people, then so be it. This is a fantasy, after all.<br /><br />That being said, the world-building is pretty fantastic all across the board. The devil is in the details or in this case, the Core, but more importantly, this is a novel all about the people in it. The good, the bad, and the ugly.<br /><br />Arlen and Leesha and the one-time weak Renna play big roles in this book, too, never fear. Arlen revisits his past and there are all kinds of awesomeness here, but what is most surprising is how cool Leesha has become, from a young wise-woman healer to a whirlwind of change to love interest of a certain warrior. Color me surprised! It just goes to show. Trust certain writers to get you there. Have faith. I do, now. :)<br /><br />But who was the most surprising?<br /><br />Renna. Meek, oft-abused Renna, subject to so much injustice... and then she's given a real chance. I think this is the point where I go from liking Arlen's martial prowess and his scholarship less and where I start viscerally appreciating him. :)<br /><br />And, as always, demon fights, demon fights, demon fights. :) Gotta love them. Really over the top cool. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5690124129624445912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1245089635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1245089635" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1245089635?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1245089635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14235744237014661766">The second lengthy entry into the Demon Cycle series...<br/><br/>There are 4 distinct sections to the book.<br/><br/>If you came into this one directly from 'The Warded Man,' you'll have to change gears rather abruptly. In the first section, we switch to the viewpoint of a minor character from 'The Warded Man,' the Krasian merchant Abban. We follow him from childhood up through the events we saw from Arlen's perspective in the first book. <br/><br/>In principle, this sounds like a good idea. I complained that in the first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText14235744237014661766" style="display:none">The second lengthy entry into the Demon Cycle series...<br /><br />There are 4 distinct sections to the book.<br /><br />If you came into this one directly from 'The Warded Man,' you'll have to change gears rather abruptly. In the first section, we switch to the viewpoint of a minor character from 'The Warded Man,' the Krasian merchant Abban. We follow him from childhood up through the events we saw from Arlen's perspective in the first book. <br /><br />In principle, this sounds like a good idea. I complained that in the first book, Krasia was too much of a two-dimensional place based solely on stereotypes about the Middle East. You would think that getting inside their culture would help. Unfortunately, it's more of the same. It continues to feel stereotypical, and becomes even more tedious when it's just a retread through events we already know about... at length.<br /><br />The second section starts 1/3 of the way through the book, and finally returns us to where we expected to be at the end of The Warded Man, following Leesha and Rojer. The third section concentrates more on Renna, and the last section brings us back more to Arlen (Mr. Warded Man himself) and demon fighting. <br /><br />The latter three sections are an improvement over the first, but they still haven't won me over. After some consideration as to the reasons - I know this is a widely acclaimed series - I think the main thing, for me, is that the book tries to address some serious issues for its characters, and creates some complex, difficult situations (including some involving rape, incest, abuse, murder, etc...) But - the way it handles those situations just feels to me rather shallow and awkward. It's earnest, but not wholly convincing. <br /><br />However, there is definitely a compelling aspect to this saga. I can understand why many fans of huge, sprawling fantasy tales endorse the series. <br /><br />Some of the sections, on their own, would have gotten three stars, but the parts set in Krasia, and the those involving Renna's family, bring this down to two for me.<br /><br />I'm not totally writing off continuing with this series, but I think I'll give it a break for a while and try a different epic fantasy next...</span>
  <a data-text-id="14235744237014661766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_444194353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444194353" />
    <a title="Cameron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2670364-cameron"><img alt="Cameron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483051477p2/2670364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444194353?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cameron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cameron" href="/user/show/2670364-cameron">Cameron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444194353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15183316235741945696">The Desert Spear isn't terribly written, but it is ultimately derivative and uninspired. Thankfully, the worst part of the novel is dealt with straightaway in its first third - specifically the mind-numbingly unoriginal Krasians, who appear to be naught but carbon copies of Islamist culture, down to their caste system and the way they treat their women. Men and women die gleefully for the glory of their God in combat. Women are kept wrapped up in shrouds. Men unable to take part in combat are sn</span>
  <span id="freeText15183316235741945696" style="display:none">The Desert Spear isn't terribly written, but it is ultimately derivative and uninspired. Thankfully, the worst part of the novel is dealt with straightaway in its first third - specifically the mind-numbingly unoriginal Krasians, who appear to be naught but carbon copies of Islamist culture, down to their caste system and the way they treat their women. Men and women die gleefully for the glory of their God in combat. Women are kept wrapped up in shrouds. Men unable to take part in combat are sneered at. Sound familiar? Yup, it did to me too.<br /><br />It really doesn't help matters much that Jadir, the secondary protagonist to the Warded Man, is far and beyond the worst stereotype in the bunch. It's a shame, too, because the world as detailed in Warded Man had great potential. And while the first novel featured three very eye-rollling Mary Sues, at least their origin stories were fascinating enough to make them likable characters. Here, the unique world feels diminished and most of the characters lack any real progress - and some, as in the case of Leesha, seem to become even more marionette-like. I'm not sure who would find the Leesha-Jardir love story at all likable, but it certainly wasn't me.<br /><br />I say "most characters" because Desert Spear does a good job with two characters - the continued adventures of the Warded Man as well as his love interest, Renna. Renna's story in particular brings back flashes of the original's interesting and decidedly more adult moments. Whereas Rojer, Leesha, and Jardir end up feeling and acting like angsty teenagers by the end of the novel, Renna and Arlen's story develops nicely. The brutality visited upon Renna is described in broad strokes, often to the benefit of the novel (as was the case with Leesha in the first). It doesn't trivialize the matters any - it just makes them easier to read, easier to stomach. There's a good sense of how far Renna's mind has stretched, and in some cases, shattered.<br /><br />I can't recommend The Desert Spear. It's too derivative and is a disappointment after the first. However, given that there are several more books left in the series, perhaps the author can turn things around. I certainly hope so. The world still has potential, if the author is willing to shy away from typical romantic and fantasy conventions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15183316235741945696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1921526478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1921526478" />
    <a title="Damien Black" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56014842-damien-black"><img alt="Damien Black" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537372504p2/56014842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1921526478?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damien Black" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damien Black" href="/user/show/56014842-damien-black">Damien Black</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007492558" href="/book/show/17320106-the-desert-spear">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1921526478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11879140280978892247">In short, this is the kind of fantasy I like to read, and the kind of fantasy I like to write: dark, done on an epic scale.<br/><br/>Brett has tapped into medieval Islamic warrior culture superbly in his follow-up to The Painted Man, and Krasian king of kings Jardir is the perfect anti-hero: ruthless and vainglorious, yet honourable to the core (no pun intended) and charming and likeable. He is the perfect foil for Arlen Bales, aka the Painted Man, who epitomises the American frontier spirit with his 'non</span>
  <span id="freeText11879140280978892247" style="display:none">In short, this is the kind of fantasy I like to read, and the kind of fantasy I like to write: dark, done on an epic scale.<br /><br />Brett has tapped into medieval Islamic warrior culture superbly in his follow-up to The Painted Man, and Krasian king of kings Jardir is the perfect anti-hero: ruthless and vainglorious, yet honourable to the core (no pun intended) and charming and likeable. He is the perfect foil for Arlen Bales, aka the Painted Man, who epitomises the American frontier spirit with his 'none of that Deliverer nonsense' approach to fighting demonkind with their own magic, and making a damn fine job of it too.<br /><br />I won't accuse Brett of doing anything so obvious as trying to reference one of the perceived great struggles of our times in his fiction, but his choice of early colonial America and early Islamic Middle East as his cultural templates does make for fascinating reading from a 21st century standpoint. <br /><br />The first section of the book is entirely devoted to developing Jardir and his irrepressible sidekick Abban (a crafty merchant who overcomes disability and disapprobation to become Jardir's right-hand man) in their efforts to consolidate first the southern desert tribes of Krasia and then the rest of humanity against the Alagai (Krasian-speak for demonkind). The tribal warrior culture into which they are born is starkly portrayed by Brett's muscular prose: harsh, brutal and hierarchical, but bold and courageous too, and I was engrossed from the off. I didn't even yearn to get back to Arlen, Leesha and the rest of the northern 'chin', it was that good.<br /><br />When Brett did finally choose to steer me back Thesa-way, I wasn't disappointed though: Renna's ongoing struggles against her abusive father Harl and Arlen's politicking among the Free Cities had me gripped, and Leesha is my kind of heroine - as smart as she is beautiful, someone who manages to be no pushover without resorting to violence. <br /><br />And of course, in a 750-page epic it was only going to be a matter of time before these two cultures - and their protagonists - clashed. No spoilers here, but some of the results were surprising, and once again, very engaging. For a fantasy author who has been accused by some of spending little time on world-building, Brett has taken great pains to depict cultural differences with verisimilude, and he had me laughing and shaking my head in equal measures as Leesha, Rojer, Jardir and his scheming sorceress first wife Inevera struggled to bridge the vast divide between them for the sake of humanity.<br /><br />And finally, watching all of this human drama with an unhuman interest we have the coreling prince... A new and even more sinister breed of demon, bent on foiling all efforts to overthrow its kind. These POV entries were few and far between, and all the more chilling for being rare.<br /><br />Brett has succeeded in conjuring up a masterpiece with his second book, one that uses the first as a springboard to reach new heights. To see a writer of this kind enjoy such success certainly gives me faith in my own endeavours, as Brett is clearly not afraid to use the genre to put all the facets of humanity under the microscope: the profane and sacred, the brave and cowardly, the selfish and selfless, the cruel and merciful, the weak and strong, are all revealed in this tour de force of epic dark fantasy that portrays the human condition in all its folly and glory.<br /><br />I'm already looking forward to the next instalment, though I'll probably wait a while before I start: I need time to recover from all that excitement!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11879140280978892247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1424369550" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424369550" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424369550?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424369550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14636603901100505962">For the past couple of days I've been trying to come up with an insightful review that would explain why this book completely changed my feelings for this series. And I'm sorry to say but... I failed.<br/><br/>My dislike for this book was such a visceral thing that I cannot really explain it. I can however point things I didn't like: <br/><br/>- The book starts with a new PoV for whom I cared little. He's also part of a middle eastern extremist type of culture, which I dislike immensely. There's lots of tiresome in</span>
  <span id="freeText14636603901100505962" style="display:none">For the past couple of days I've been trying to come up with an insightful review that would explain why this book completely changed my feelings for this series. And I'm sorry to say but... I failed.<br /><br />My dislike for this book was such a visceral thing that I cannot really explain it. I can however point things I didn't like: <br /><br />- The book starts with a new PoV for whom I cared little. He's also part of a middle eastern extremist type of culture, which I dislike immensely. There's lots of tiresome intrigues and time-jumps and I found myself caring less and less as time went by.<br /><br />- When we finally go back to our old main characters there's a lot of romance and drama that wasn't there before. Suddenly everyone is finding new partners and some of them (Arlen's in particular) are just annoying. <br /><br />Sorry, but nope. Not continuing with this series after this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14636603901100505962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_132859684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132859684" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480301169p2/2517340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132859684?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176879-the-desert-spear">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132859684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3678434199408175560">In the past I've been called a "book slut", and I don't argue this title. I read a lot of books, and I'm not hard to please. But I've been thinking lately.. Maybe the better term for me might be "book nympho". You see, I enjoy reading, all reading, good or bad. Where as a "book slut" might read a lot of books, any books really, they might not necessarily enjoy reading them. The whole time they are reading they are looking for something in particular. They read to critique, to pick a book apart, </span>
  <span id="freeText3678434199408175560" style="display:none">In the past I've been called a "book slut", and I don't argue this title. I read a lot of books, and I'm not hard to please. But I've been thinking lately.. Maybe the better term for me might be "book nympho". You see, I enjoy reading, all reading, good or bad. Where as a "book slut" might read a lot of books, any books really, they might not necessarily enjoy reading them. The whole time they are reading they are looking for something in particular. They read to critique, to pick a book apart, always looking for that next great book to fill the bookless empty part of their soul, but never quite finding a perfect fit. A "book nympho" on the other hand.. Enjoys reading. Any reading. Some books are much better <s>in bed</s> to read than others, but they still enjoy the act of reading the ones that aren't as good, they overlook flaws and things that might annoy others, because they get caught up in the act of reading and just want more more moremoremoremoremore. <br /><br />*ahem*<br /><br />So yes. I, Dawn, am a book nympho. <i>Hi Dawn</i>.<br /><br />I'm not sure why I decided to share all of that in this review... I guess because in the last couple months I've become sort of a book slut. I've started countless books, only to lose interest and put them down. It's not that they weren't good books, I'm sure I'll get back to them and finish them someday (and I'll probably love them, I mean hello, book nympho). But for the last couple of months nothing could capture me, distract me, draw me in and hold me.<br /><br />And then I picked up The Desert Spear, and something funny happened. I would read it.. Put it down... And find myself <i>wanting</i> to pick it back up. I should probably mention that I gave Painted/Warded Man five stars as well. I loved it when I read it, so if you didn't at least like it as well, this review probably won't help you decide whether or not to read Desert Spear. But if you at least liked Painted/Warded Man.. Give Desert Spear a try. I said I rated Painted/Warded Man five stars.. Now I kind of wish I had rated it four. Because after reading Desert Spear? I liked it so much more. It was just a great ride, cover to cover.<br /><br />New and interesting POV's, a teeny tiny bit of romance (not too much, just enough to sate my girlish desires, don't worry guys), a little sex even (but damn you Brett, not nearly detailed enough, *shakes fist*). The characters from Painted/Warded Man are back as well, and I felt more connected to them this time around.. Maybe just because that's what typically happens in a series; you have more time to get to know characters and therefore feel for them more in times of joy or sorrow. But I think it's also a testament to Brett's story telling ability. <br /><br />All in all.. Loved it. I'm so glad I finally found a book to kick me out of my reading slump. Thanks Mr. Brett, I can't wait for the next installment in the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3678434199408175560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AF7gXWfCnjRP3xOHKzPWvWgFSCK8zR4fH7AsY44yz6doEvyhujYJSe7v1HO9imRP1z/r/3lsTVLH6I7iIg8Lbw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tDJR71Ln0DxnTHj2CHC9XtJha1Agnv7aVSemV4Uqzgrcfk0TjxNHQcZ8vwKeyQ+sbVvIjeU/rZeNfwTWKRcKwg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2638695461542904558">Peter V. Brett is the internationally bestselling author of the Demon Cycle series, which has sold over two million copies in 25 languages worldwide. Novels include The Warded Man, The Desert Spear, The Daylight War, The Skull Throne, and The Core. Other works include the Red Sonja: Unchained graphic novel and the Demon Cycle novellas The Great Bazaar, Brayan's Gold, Messenger's Legacy, and Barren</span>
  <span id="freeText2638695461542904558" style="display:none">Peter V. Brett is the internationally bestselling author of the Demon Cycle series, which has sold over two million copies in 25 languages worldwide. Novels include The Warded Man, The Desert Spear, The Daylight War, The Skull Throne, and The Core. Other works include the Red Sonja: Unchained graphic novel and the Demon Cycle novellas The Great Bazaar, Brayan's Gold, Messenger's Legacy, and Barren.
